    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_465200641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/465200641" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/465200641?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525425915" href="/book/show/12842115-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465200641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9070071695049809352">After reading and loving <b>If I Stay</b> and <b>Where She Went</b> by Gayle Forman, I was thrilled to hear Ms. Forman was working on a new novel, <b>Just One Day</b>. Just One Day was a bittersweet story that entranced me, took hold of my heart, and gave it a great big <i>squeeze</i>! My heart still aches. <br/><br/>Allyson is almost to the end of her graduation present, a three week trip touring Europe. She’s spent the time speed traveling through Europe, and is now in London on the last leg of the trip. On a whim and an accident,</span>
  <span id="freeText9070071695049809352" style="display:none">After reading and loving <b>If I Stay</b> and <b>Where She Went</b> by Gayle Forman, I was thrilled to hear Ms. Forman was working on a new novel, <b>Just One Day</b>. Just One Day was a bittersweet story that entranced me, took hold of my heart, and gave it a great big <i>squeeze</i>! My heart still aches. <br /><br />Allyson is almost to the end of her graduation present, a three week trip touring Europe. She’s spent the time speed traveling through Europe, and is now in London on the last leg of the trip. On a whim and an accident, she meets charismatic Willem, a Dutch actor at the end of his tour performing the Shakespearian play, Twelfth Night. There is an instant connection and attraction. When he finds out that Allyson missed Paris and is about to travel home without seeing it, he insists she go there with him as her guide. Normally Allyson would never do such a thing. Break her plans, and do something spur of the moment and with a total stranger? No way. But the past few weeks of let down and disappointment from her trip have worn her down, and she’s ready to take a leap into the unknown. They spend an amazing and strange day together, and an incredible night, but when Allyson wakes, Willem is gone and left no clue where to find him. <br /><br />Shattered, she goes home and tries to plunge into college but she just can’t shake the pain. Added to that, Allyson is enrolled in classes basically picked by her mother as a pre-med student. That one day doing as she pleased in Paris, had more of a profound effect on her than she realized, and she just can’t stomach going along with other’s expectations anymore. <br /><br />This story broke my heart! The first third of the book had a dreamy but achy quality to it, because she’s spending this amazing but intense day with Willem, and you know it won’t last. She’s going home, and so is he, but I didn’t expect for him to just up and leave her! At that point on Allyson basically goes through a big depression and I felt like I went through it with her. As heartbreaking as the experience was, doing the unexpected was liberating for Allyson, and soon she starts to question what she really wants out of life. <br /><br />I felt so bad for Allyson, I felt like she was bullied by her mother and her “friend,” Melanie. Spending time with these two sucked the confidence and will right out of her. I really couldn’t stand Melanie. At the beginning of the trip she was nothing but an attention hog, and put Allyson down continually. The mother was another character I couldn’t stand. She poured her own expectations into Allyson instead of letting her find what was right for her. I hate to say this, but I didn’t like Willem for most of the book either, and it seemed the more I found out about him, the more I hated him. However, hold that thought and don’t let that sway you too much against him. There is more to his story. Still, it wasn’t enough for me to like him,..…..yet. I’m hoping I see a completely different side of things from him in the next book, which apparently is in his POV. I hope to find out that appearances were misleading. I hope this for Allyson, and well, for me too! You know me, I want that happy ending. <br /><br />Don’t read this if you haven’t read <b>If I Stay</b>. I have to think back to my feelings when I read it, and remember that for most of the story I had this achy feeling, as well. Yes, Adam and Mia loved each other, but looming ahead of them were their futures, which were about to take a very different and separate path. Even without the accident, they had a tough road ahead, and I kept wondering how things were going to work. This was multiplied tenfold when I started <b>Where She Went</b> and found out what happened! But tsk, tsk, ye of little faith (yes, that was me). Of course Gayle Forman made it right, and the heartbreak only made the end SO MUCH SWEETER! So I HAVE to believe this is what she will do here. Work her magic and heal my heart. We shall see. I will leave off with a swoony quote to soothe some of the heartache: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“As if disconnected to the rest of my body, my hand raises in the air and goes to touch his cheek. But before it arrives, Willem’s hand whips around and grabs my wrist. For one confused second, I think I’ve misread the situation again, am about to be refused. Willem holds my wrist for a long moment, looking at that birthmark. Then he lifts it to his mouth. And though his lips are soft and his kiss is gentle, it feels like a knife jamming into the electrical socket. It feels like the moment I go live.”* </i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Quotes are taken from an uncorrected proof and may change in the final copy.</i><br /><br />You can read this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/12/review-just-one-day-by-gayle-forman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9070071695049809352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-favorite">2013-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=penguin">penguin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-own-it">i-own-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417760176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17470745213613068317">I'm really starting to think I need to spend more time in the Contemporary genre. While I'm there I might as well finally read <em>If I Stay</em> and <em>Where She Went.</em> Yes, I can't believe I haven't read them yet either. No, I'm not sure what my malfunction is. But what I am sure of is how happy I am to have finally read a Gayle Forman novel. <em>Just One Day</em> came complete with a charming cast of characters, Parisian backdrop and such a relatable coming of age story.<br/><br/>Right from the start I knew I would love thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17470745213613068317" style="display:none">I'm really starting to think I need to spend more time in the Contemporary genre. While I'm there I might as well finally read <em>If I Stay</em> and <em>Where She Went.</em> Yes, I can't believe I haven't read them yet either. No, I'm not sure what my malfunction is. But what I am sure of is how happy I am to have finally read a Gayle Forman novel. <em>Just One Day</em> came complete with a charming cast of characters, Parisian backdrop and such a relatable coming of age story.<br><br>Right from the start I knew I would love this book. Allyson reminds me so much of my younger self. She's unsure of herself, follows the rules to the T, is more focused on the approval of other around her verses what she wants, etc. I'm sure we could all relate to feeling that way at one point in our lives and that's what made this book real for me. While Allyson is traveling Europe with her teen tour group, she stumbles across Willem, who seems to be the opposite of herself. So for just one day, Allyson decides take a few chances, takes up the alter ego "Lulu" and becomes the spontaneous traveler.<br><br>I totally get that. Sometimes you just want to take a page from Nike and JUST DO IT. Even still today, I get those urges of just letting go and let live. But then, the next thing I know things have gotten so widely out of control.<br><br><img alt="neat_freak_fail-123529" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391735i/754282.jpg" width="336" height="251" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And soon after, I'm once again craving my comfort box.<br><br><img alt="comfort box" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391735i/754283.jpg" width="350" height="329" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But enough about me...<br><br>What I loved about <em>Just One Day</em> is how Allyson both loses herself that day in Paris and later finds herself over the course of a year afterwards. When all is said and done and she has to resume her life after being left by Willem, she's broken, a mere shadow of who she thought she was. I think it was there that I truly started to connect with Allyson on a deeper level. Here we have a former honor student struggling to get by in her college courses, struggling to keep former relationships intact and struggling at making new ones. What I found most interesting is that it's not her relationship with Willem that metaphorically heals her, but the secondary characters she meets at college. How often do we read in YA novels the male heart-throb being the catalyst for change in the heroine? Too often, in my opinion. Allyson's change is gradual and is due to various people and experiences, most of which have nothing to do with Willem. Ya know, pretty much how life is supposed to work.<br><br>I went into this story expecting some sort of fluffy romantic contemporary novel, but I guess I should have known it wouldn't be that simple. I suppose that's what I get for being fashionably late to the Gayle Forman party. *dons her party hat* What I got was a novel that really examines that feeling of uncertainty of who we choose to be, how others perceive us, and how those two situations are sometimes mutually exclusive. The feeling of enlightenment I had with <em>Just One Day</em> was very similar to how I felt while reading <em><a title="ARC Book Review: Wanderlove by Kirsten Hubbard" href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2012/02/20/arc-book-review-wanderlove-by-kirsten-hubbard/" rel="nofollow noopener">Wanderlove</a>,</em> which also features a girl searching for answers, but ends up finding so much more.<br><br>Then, of course, you have the fantastic setting of Paris. I've always wanted to go to Paris and one day I intend to. But while I was reading, it was so easy to visualize the french cafes, the old buildings, the culture. This is the second travel type novel I've read and it's a wonderful change in scenery. High school angst vs. Europe. I think we know who wins that round.<br><br>If there is one thing I have to nitpick, it'd be the ending. Not that it was bad, but I think it has more to do with personal tastes. It's also where I found myself conflicted. Right after finishing<em> Just One Day</em>, I felt I needed more, that I wasn't completely satisfied with the ending. I wanted her to find Willem and to figure out what happened. But on further reflection I realized something. This wasn't about Willem. It was about Allyson finding herself. So clever, Forman. But I still want to know what happens after that door opens. So, I think it goes without saying that I'll be needing <em><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842134-just-one-year" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Year</a>.</em> Heh.<br><br>I love novels that take me away from the usual and make me think. <em>Just One Day</em> was just what I needed. Refreshing, humorous and deep.<br><br><i>ARC was received from the publisher for and honest review. Thank you, PenguinTeen!</i><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17470745213613068317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_221472908" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221472908" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221472908?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17250987-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221472908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3956525255354049854"><b>Post reading thoughts:</b> Oh gosh this book just took my heart and stomped all over it. I <i>need</i> Just One Year now! Full review to come once I've got all my feelings in check.<br/><br/>Please excuse my meagre attempt at gathering my chaotic thoughts and trying to write a coherent review, but Just One Day just evoked so many different emotions within me. So many books come around that leave just a deep lasting impression and without a doubt Just One Day is one of those books.<br/><br/>Allyson was meant to be on trip of h</span>
  <span id="freeText3956525255354049854" style="display:none"><b>Post reading thoughts:</b> Oh gosh this book just took my heart and stomped all over it. I <i>need</i> Just One Year now! Full review to come once I've got all my feelings in check.<br /><br />Please excuse my meagre attempt at gathering my chaotic thoughts and trying to write a coherent review, but Just One Day just evoked so many different emotions within me. So many books come around that leave just a deep lasting impression and without a doubt Just One Day is one of those books.<br /><br />Allyson was meant to be on trip of her life in Europe, but it didn’t have that life changing effect as she was hoping. Her best friend Mel kept encouraging her to enjoy herself and make the most out of it. But Allyson wasn’t like Mel, constantly taking risks; the only big risk Allyson had taken so far was cut her hair to a bob. But on their last night in London on their tour, Allyson and Mel decide not to follow the rules and watch a different production of a play and that’s where she meets Willem, she knows there’s something about him as soon as their eyes meet in the pit of her stomach. The next day when she meets him on the train, she makes a spur of the moment decision to travel to Paris with him for just one day. He’s a complete stranger but Allyson finds herself wanting to take this chance and do something normal Allyson wouldn’t do.<br /><br />This one day ends up being an epitome of what her entire trip in Europe was meant to be about. Willem tries to encapsulate the beautiful experience of Paris for Allyson, but she ends up with leaving more than she bargained for, that would affect her whole outlook on life months later, returning to the US Allyson is a changed person.<br /><br />The last time I felt so much love for a book was when I read Gayle Forman’s Where She Went in Just One Day. Just One Day had the same achy, raw lingering effect on me but it was that much more profound. It was like I was on my own journey of discovery and growth with Allyson, I was led to believe so much about Willem that I felt the same amount of fury and heartache that Allyson did. When she was lost and hurt afterwards and when she finally started doing things for herself instead of being dictated at her whole entire life. I felt like Andy Murray at Wimbledon getting pumped up by the crowd and continually pumping my fist. (And I never do this) It’s like Gayle had this magical wand when writing this book and just knew how to push your buttons that I found myself so involved with Allyson’s life that I wanted so much for her to get her happy ending.<br /><br />Allyson’s personal growth over the course of the book was so admirable it was like she was shedding her skin until she finally found the real Allyson underneath. I liked watching her friendships blossom especially with Dee (I wasn’t really a fan of Mel), take the courage to do what she wanted and knew she had to in her heart.<br /><br />Willem was a complete enigma, at times I was never sure who the real Willem was, I thought I was able to get glances of him, but he was quick to cover up his true feelings. But like Allyson I wasn’t able to resist his charms. I like how there’s so many complicated layers to this guy, so much we haven’t touched upon and I am beyond eager at unravelling all this mystery when we get his pov in Just One Year.<br /><br />Gayle Forman has once again created such a heartbreaking realistic read that resonated with me. For me she has taken her writing up in a whole another notch from Where She Went, I found myself constantly highlighting my favourite quotes (which was pretty much the entire book) and re-reading favourite passages over and over again.<br /><br />This journey that I was able to take with Allyson over the course of this beautiful book will be one I won’t forget. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3956525255354049854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_451879382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451879382" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/451879382?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525425915" href="/book/show/12842115-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=romance-contemporary">romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451879382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12917383205345182577">My rating: 3 of 5 stars<br/>A copy of Just One Day was provided to me by Dutton/Penguin Group (USA) for review purposes.<br/><br/><i>'We are born in one day. We die in one day. We can change in one day. And we can fall in love in one day. Anything can happen in just one day.'</i><br/><br/>Admittedly, I do believe I started this when I was in the completely wrong sort of mood. I totally killed this story for myself in the beginning and could not get into it. I was mentally flashing to scenes from 'Taken' and kept waiting for he</span>
  <span id="freeText12917383205345182577" style="display:none">My rating: 3 of 5 stars<br>A copy of Just One Day was provided to me by Dutton/Penguin Group (USA) for review purposes.<br><br><i>'We are born in one day. We die in one day. We can change in one day. And we can fall in love in one day. Anything can happen in just one day.'</i><br><br>Admittedly, I do believe I started this when I was in the completely wrong sort of mood. I totally killed this story for myself in the beginning and could not get into it. I was mentally flashing to scenes from 'Taken' and kept waiting for her to start using her brain and NOT get on the train with the complete stranger BY HERSELF to PARIS where she's never been before, barely has any money, and can't speak the language. I can understand getting caught up in the moment and feeling a connection to someone so much that you just lose yourself in the moment... but this was just downright reckless and so potentially dangerous that it sucked all enjoyment out of it for me.<br><br>Allyson was such a strange and unrealistic narrator. Always the smart girl, the girl who played it safe, and then she meets Willem and he unlocks a side of her that she herself didn't know existed. Allyson had been on a tour of Europe for several weeks but had never got to see Paris, so he asks for her to go with him there. And this is where I get even MORE disturbed. They have one single day in Paris and it ended up being the most random, jumbled and seemingly unenjoyable day. So it wasn't the type of day spent in Paris like you see in the movies but they didn't even DO anything! So much beauty surrounded them and for part of it they ended up taking a nap in the park? Are you kidding me? If I had a single day in Paris and I needed to nap I'd be pounding the red bulls and trying to get the most I could out of that day.<br><br><i>'We kiss again. This next kiss is the kind that breaks open the sky. It steals my breath and gives it back. It shows me that every other kiss I've had in my life has been wrong.'</i><br><br>I’m not saying that it’s impossible to meet someone and only after a single day they have somehow managed to change a piece of you forever. I believe that can happen; I’ve felt it. But I didn’t feel it while reading this and I was left dumbfounded and confused to what Willem did exactly to evoke such a long-lasting reaction. I just didn’t’ believe it strongly enough. My other issue was with the fact that she attributed this other her, “Lulu”, as a result of being with Willem. It was disheartening to see her give up that new her just because he disappeared. I would have liked to see her take the situation for what it was: a life lesson that opened her eyes to how different she could live her life and actually enjoy it in the process. But instead she crawled deeper into her shell than she had before. <br><br>The Ending. Spoilers! For real. Don't click.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I found the ending to be a bit of an eye roll, to be honest. After all that and it was just one big misunderstanding and he had likely just gone out to get them breakfast?? And then he gets detoured because he winds up in the hospital requiring stitches? (My theory is that those guys ended up catching him after all.) Meanwhile, Allyson is flailing around Paris because she was sure he had abandoned her. And then she spends the next year dwelling on it and why he left her? I don’t know, I just didn’t buy it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Of course I have to read the follow-up because it’s obvious that Allyson was lacking in answers and I can only hope we receive some resolution (that is logical too) from Willem’s side of things. And hello cliffhanger, thanks for that. Not terribly pleased with the story itself but there’s really no denying it, Gayle Forman can write one entrancing story.<br><br>*All quotes taken are from an uncorrected proof*<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" title="Sweet Tidbits" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351064i/704765.gif" alt="Sweet Tidbits" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_438310752" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438310752" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438310752?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525425915" href="/book/show/12842115-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=highly-anticipating-2013">highly-anticipating-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=hand-me-some-tissues">hand-me-some-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=gimme-the-next-book">gimme-the-next-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438310752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6235932351331002878">Actual Rating: 4.5 stars<br/><br/>Quite a few months ago, in my early reviewing days, when I was just a new face in the world of reviewing and book blogging, I read a book called <i>Die for Me</i>. Although it had an interesting and original premise (which, ultimately, was revealed to be poorly executed), a pretty cover, and some mixed to positive reviews from friends of mine, the main reason I really wanted to read <i>Die for Me</i> was because it took place in Paris, and I'd hoped that the author would take advantage</span>
  <span id="freeText6235932351331002878" style="display:none">Actual Rating: 4.5 stars<br /><br />Quite a few months ago, in my early reviewing days, when I was just a new face in the world of reviewing and book blogging, I read a book called <i>Die for Me</i>. Although it had an interesting and original premise (which, ultimately, was revealed to be poorly executed), a pretty cover, and some mixed to positive reviews from friends of mine, the main reason I really wanted to read <i>Die for Me</i> was because it took place in Paris, and I'd hoped that the author would take advantage of such a wonderful and rich setting. Unfortunately, the most background of Paris the author provided us readers with in <i>Die for Me</i> was the Metro and a few coffee shops. Maybe a lake or two. Some really great details of Paris in that book, you guys. <br /><br />Since then, I've been wary of books taking place in Paris. Until, however, <i>Just One Day</i> appeared on my feed. Written by an incredibly hyped author and receiving rave early reviews, I figured that Forman could do no wrong with the beautiful Paris.<br /><br />And I was right. <br /><br />I'd gone into <i>Just One Day</i> with expectations of heartbreak, high levels of swoon, awe-worthy prose and a strong, overwhelming desire to hop on a plane to Paris immediately. And while all of those expectations were met, and in fact exceeded, I came across quite a few surprises along the way - such as the fact that <i>Just One Day</i> is filled with truly hysterical passages and moments - which I don't say very often about books, especially not about books in the YA genre, considering the fact that I have the sense of humor that will have me inevitably burning in hell, and most YA novels don't cross that particular boundary to meet my sense of humor - and the fact that I'd be so engaged with Allyson and Willem's travels in such a short amount of time. <br /><br />Allyson was, for the most part, an awesome and incredibly witty character, and in the end, I am definitely able to say that I enjoyed reading in her perspective and seeing her character meet such a large amount of growth throughout the course of the novel. While she did, at times, get on my nerves - most notably how she got jealous whenever a girl looked at Willem, or whenever a girl talked to Willem after knowing him for just one day <s>(oh look, I've used the title of the book in my review! This is almost as exciting as when the title of a movie is spoken in said movie.)</s>, she eventually ended up winning me over once again with her wit and snark. Willem was also an amazing character, and while he wasn't met with very much growth at all throughout the course of <i>Just One Day</i>, I thoroughly enjoyed the scenes where he opened up to Allyson - however slightly - about his home life, even after knowing her for such a short period of time. <br /><br />Charming, often hysterical, with some great characters, equally as great relationship dynamics, and a clever incorporation of Shakespeare, <i>Just One Day</i> is not a novel to be missed for anyone looking for a quick and incredibly fun read that makes you feel like you're roaming the streets of Paris. If you had asked me before reading this novel if two people can fall in love in just one day, I probably would have lectured you about the vast difference between lust and love, but after reading this novel and experiencing the relationship that is Allyson and Willem's firsthand, my opinion may have been swayed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6235932351331002878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2422468807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2422468807" />
    <a title="Mackenzie Lane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26303598-mackenzie-lane"><img alt="Mackenzie Lane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559203827p2/26303598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2422468807?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie Lane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie Lane" href="/user/show/26303598-mackenzie-lane">Mackenzie Lane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=not-my-cup-of-tea">not-my-cup-of-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=over-hyped">over-hyped</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422468807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2162949562343938220">Lol soooooo this is gonna be interesting. Suffice it to say, I don't really care for <i>Just One Day.</i><br/>Or Allyson. Or Willem. <br/><br/>My biggest issue, and the source of all my problems with the book, is the <b>instalove</b>. DO NOT even <i>try</i> to tell me this book doesn't have instalove, because it does, and the fact that it takes place in <b>PARIS</b>, a city I would very much like to visit someday because of my undying love and adoration for it, really ticked me off. Like, Allyson and Willem's "love affair" should've take</span>
  <span id="freeText2162949562343938220" style="display:none">Lol soooooo this is gonna be interesting. Suffice it to say, I don't really care for <i>Just One Day.</i><br />Or Allyson. Or Willem. <br /><br />My biggest issue, and the source of all my problems with the book, is the <b>instalove</b>. DO NOT even <i>try</i> to tell me this book doesn't have instalove, because it does, and the fact that it takes place in <b>PARIS</b>, a city I would very much like to visit someday because of my undying love and adoration for it, really ticked me off. Like, Allyson and Willem's "love affair" should've taken place in a dumpster for all the value it added to the overall story of Allyson's "coming-of-age" character arc.<br /><br />And what was up with Willem only ever calling Allyson "Lulu" JUST BECAUSE he thought she looked like some actress named Louise Brooks, and SHE WENT ALONG WITH IT?? Because she thought by being called a different name, she'd therefore <i>be</i> someone different? *eye rolling, but the eye roll that actually kind of strains your eyes for a few painful seconds*<br /><br />So, if you couldn't gather by the title, Allyson spends a day in Paris with Willem, a boy she just met the night before after watching him perform in a traveling Shakespeare acting group. She literally had no idea who he was before, not even a friend of a friend of a friend. Like, no clue. <br />And after their <i>*amazing*</i> day together, he's gone by the time she wakes up (after having slept together in an art studio &amp; also where "a condom materializes" - pg. 128 of <i>Just One Day</i>) and <b>Allyson not only refuses to get over Willem, but cries the whole way home and for the next <i>year</i></b>. Pretty much. I mean, until she goes back to Paris <b>looking for him</b>. I mean, can you fault someone for such persistence? Lol sure looks like I am.<br /><br />Now, the end is actually my favorite part of the book. And by favorite, I mean the part I found least annoying. Well, until that asinine cliff-hanger.... But her exploring Paris <i>without</i> Willem, was better than when she was there with him, even if she was only in Paris a second time to search for Willem. <br /><br />Here are some brief examples of what helped this story fall flat for me:<br /><br /> - <b>Willem licks Allyson's blood from his own finger</b>. ONLY KNEW EACH OTHER FOR A DAY, FOLKS. disgusting and repulsive, it was. sexy and alluring, it was <i>not</i>.<br /> - <b>The chase scene after Allyson hits a random dude in the head with a book because she "instinctively" knew they were trouble after seeing girls scream bloody murder in their presence</b>. And the fact that Allyson and Willem outran them. This was a highly unlikely scene, and the absurdity of it all made me yell about it to my mom, to whom I am most sorry. But she agreed with me, so <i>there</i>.<br /> - <b>"...stopping to drink at the pool of my clavicle..." - pg. 127</b>. If there's a more unappealing way of writing a first kiss/make-out/sex scene (because they do all of the above in one go), I'd be flabbergasted. I mean, calling it a "collarbone" would be a slight improvement, but not a substantial one.<br /> - <b> "Willem gives me that look of his..." - pg. 90</b> What look of his? Need I remind you, Allyson/Lulu, YOU HAVE JUST MET THIS BOY. There is absolutely no way you know his looks. That's something people only pick up on with time. Unfortunately, that's the one thing the author couldn't grant you &amp; Willem, and the only thing that would've made this entire freaking story believable. No lie, if Allyson &amp; Willem would've spent at least a week together, I probably would have loved the crap out of this book. Eh...maybe.<br /> - <b>THE YEAR WITHOUT WILLEM</b>. Literally Allyson spent all her time/money/effort/ and all her friends' time/money/effort to search for Willem because she couldn't just MOVE ON. And when any supporting character was spouting truth at Allyson, she'd brush it off &amp; continue in her perpetual state of grief. Honestly, I found Dee, Melanie, and Wren the best characters this book had to offer. I want a book about Wren's travels, with flashbacks to when Francesca was still alive. And Winston seemed promising and supportive! At least Wren knew Winston for longer than a <b>freaking day!</b><br /> - <b>The incessant talk of "electricity"</b>. I would love to get a word count of "electric" or "electricity" in this book. I'd be shocked if it wasn't used at least 50 times.<br /><br />By the end, Allyson has "found herself", but I couldn't help remembering she did all of this because of a boy. she. only. knew. for. just. one. day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2162949562343938220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_221568963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221568963" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221568963?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525425915" href="/book/show/12842115-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221568963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7198245010866760111"><b>Rating Clarification: 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>“We are born in one day. We die in one day. We can change in one day. And we can fall in love in one day. Anything can happen in just one day.”</i> This is a quote from an uncorrected proof.<br/><br/><b>Just One Day</b> by Gayle Forman is what I would consider a worthy start to what I truly believe will have an epic continuation. This book delivered in all the ways Forman knows how, which is a great premise, a likable cast and a primer for a promising part two. I think the early reader</span>
  <span id="freeText7198245010866760111" style="display:none"><b>Rating Clarification: 3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>“We are born in one day. We die in one day. We can change in one day. And we can fall in love in one day. Anything can happen in just one day.”</i> This is a quote from an uncorrected proof.<br /><br /><b>Just One Day</b> by Gayle Forman is what I would consider a worthy start to what I truly believe will have an epic continuation. This book delivered in all the ways Forman knows how, which is a great premise, a likable cast and a primer for a promising part two. I think the early readers of <b>If I Stay</b> will agree with me when I say we never considered the possibility that Forman would deliver a second installment to her beloved novel. I, for one, was ecstatic to hear she would continue Mia’s story, and when I stumbled upon the final pages of <b>Where She Went</b>, I was left with a feeling of pure bliss and cemented fandom for this author’s stories.<br /><br />To hear she was coming out with a new novel, <b>Just One Day</b>, had me pulling out my dancing shoes and running in circles in pure excitement. When an author earns your attention and continues to deliver greatness, there seems to be an assumed allegiance that earns them a guaranteed audience. I can comfortably declare that with a handful of authors such as Marchetta, Dessen, Green to name a few, Forman has me at “Hello.”<br /><br /><b>Just One Day</b> tells us the story of Allyson Healey who is suppose to be enjoying a life changing experience as she travels Europe with her best friend Melanie the summer before they both start college. As the trip progresses, Allyson struggles to find enjoyment in the trip until she comes across a Shakespearian Dutch actor, Willem, who sweeps her off her feet and delivers one of the most memorable days she could wish for. That changing event comes to a devastating halt when she wakes up the following morning to find he’s gone and left no means of contacting him. She returns home and goes on to start college, but she can’t seem to move past the shock of having come so close to happiness to only see it slip through her fingers.<br /><br />I have to admit I struggled to like Allyson and Willem for a portion of the novel. However, I think that was a bit purposeful on Forman’s part because if she shows all of her cards early on, the possibilities of where the story can go is cut short. I remember feeling the same way about Mia in the second installment of <b>Where She Went</b>, but I have to commend Forman for challenging her readers to keep an open mind, don’t jump to conclusions and consider the possibilities. I recommend that to those who read this novel. Despite what you deduce of these two characters, don’t sell them short because as you peel away the layers of this intricate story, you’ll find a whole new element ready to reveal itself.<br /><br />In addition, the story somewhat left me craving for more secondary character time. There were a couple of hidden gems I wanted to learn more about including Dee and Wren. I felt like I was just getting to know Dee and his story when he was suddenly placed on the sidelines. The same felt true for Wren, so I’m looking forward to revisiting these two sometime soon.<br /><br />I appreciated the themes Forman weaved into her novel around self awareness, growth and the pain of losing the possibility of what could have been. Those are topics that seem to always resonate with me, and Forman is great at delivering valuable considerations that shouldn’t be ignored.<br /><br />Overall, as much as I liked this book to a certain degree, I’m more excited to see where it will lead with the next installment when Willam takes the stage in <b>Just One Year</b>. Good book that her fans are sure to enjoy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7198245010866760111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1846035432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846035432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9188470746732454473"><u>
  <b>2nd read: January 2020 </b>
</u><br/><i>3 stars </i><br/><br/> This book felt like 3 separate and distinct books in one to me, so I decided to review it as such. Overall, I quite enjoyed it- but not as much as my initial reading in 2017. <br/><br/>Part One: <b>Allyson and the French Kiss</b><br/><i>4 stars</i><br/>Allyson is on a European trip, but despite her best efforts, is not having a great time. The more excited she is for a new city, the more movies she has seen about it- the more disappointed she is. So, when she and her friend sneak out to see a </span>
  <span id="freeText9188470746732454473" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>2nd read: January 2020 </b>
</u><br /><i>3 stars </i><br /><br /> This book felt like 3 separate and distinct books in one to me, so I decided to review it as such. Overall, I quite enjoyed it- but not as much as my initial reading in 2017. <br /><br />Part One: <b>Allyson and the French Kiss</b><br /><i>4 stars</i><br />Allyson is on a European trip, but despite her best efforts, is not having a great time. The more excited she is for a new city, the more movies she has seen about it- the more disappointed she is. So, when she and her friend sneak out to see a travelling troupe of Shakespeare performers, and a mysterious actor flicks her a coin (apparently that is the height of romance?), she is thrust into a crazy adventure that winds up with her and said mysterious actor going to Paris for- you guessed it- <i>Just One Day. </i><br /><br />Part Two: <b>Allyson and the Crushing Depression &amp; Denial</b><br /><i>2.5 stars</i><br />After a shock turn of events, Allyson is at college and… whatever the opposite of thriving is. <br /><br />I liked Allyson’s character growth throughout this section, and even though it was at times <i>very </i>frustrating I can appreciate how real it is. <br /><br />I also loved seeing someone <i>not loving </i>college. So many people say college/uni is the best time of your life. Allyson aced high school, getting straight A’s, having a good relationship with her teachers. As her guidance councillor says, it is often those people who struggle the most come their tertiary education. She started her college career as Pre-Med with high exceptions placed on her by not only her parents, but Allyson herself. But maybe that isn’t the right path. <br /><br />This book showed really the fine line between work and life placed on college/uni kids. You should study, but you should have a social life- but not too much, because <b>you have to do well in order to Have A Good Life™</b> Talk about pressure.<br /><br />Part Three: <b> Allyson and the Happy Ever After</b> <br /><i>3.5 stars</i><br />After somehow becoming fluent in French in like 3 months- Allyson travels back to where this all began. The city of lights, Paris! <br /><br />I really enjoyed this section of this story, especially after the doom and gloom the last. All the payoff from slowly seeing her progress as a character finally comes. She becomes more confident in herself, yay for self acceptance!<br /><br />She stays at a youth hostel with a group of Australian tourists. I listened to the audiobook and the Aussie accents were hilarious. They weren't the worst I have ever heard, but it felt as if the narrator studied for them by listening to Crocodile Dundee and Kath &amp; Kim.<br /><br /><b> Overall thoughts </b> <br />I really didn’t like ‘If I stay’ and then sequel ‘Where She Went’ even less. For that reason, I am pretty nervous to try the sequel 'Just One Year', but I'll give it a shot! I am glad I liked this one, even though it was slightly disappointing from what my younger self hyped it up to be. Overall, it was a fun, dramatic story about self acceptance, and finding yourself. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>1st read: June 2017 </b>
</u><br /><i>4 stars </i><br /><br /><i>"I read this while reading three books at once, as an ebook. I enjoyed it- and was, and still am, in suspense. I have LOTS of questions I want answers to and hope they are revealed in the second book."</i><br /><b>- from my 13 year old diary </b>pls don't judge (hopefully my reviewing skills have increased since then lol)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1032168890169377000">***2.5 well written stars***<br/><br/><b>JUST ONE DAY</b> is the first book for me by this author. I have a lot of friends who love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay__If_I_Stay___1_' title='If I Stay (If I Stay, #1) by Gayle Forman' rel='nofollow noopener'>If I Stay</a> so I thought I would give her new series a try. <br/><br/>Reading this story I realized something about myself - I like my characters to be together. The characters were separated at 35% and didn't reunite until <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ the very last page and it was a cliffhanger ending. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> For <u>my taste</u> that was too long and boring for it to be told in one POV and not know what </span>
  <span id="freeText1032168890169377000" style="display:none">***2.5 well written stars***<br><br><b>JUST ONE DAY</b> is the first book for me by this author. I have a lot of friends who love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay__If_I_Stay___1_" title="If I Stay (If I Stay, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a> so I thought I would give her new series a try. <br><br>Reading this story I realized something about myself - I like my characters to be together. The characters were separated at 35% and didn't reunite until <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the very last page and it was a cliffhanger ending. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> For <u>my taste</u> that was too long and boring for it to be told in one POV and not know what was happening with the other character.<blockquote>
  <b>We are born in one day. We die one day. We can change in one day. And we can fall in love in one day. Anything can happen in just one day.</b>
</blockquote><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17623975.Just_One_Day__Just_One_Day___1_" title="Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1368722144s/17623975.jpg" alt="Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842134.Just_One_Year__Just_One_Day___2_" title="Just One Year (Just One Day, #2) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1375129683s/12842134.jpg" alt="Just One Year (Just One Day, #2) by Gayle Forman" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Cliffhanger<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1032168890169377000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_222359799" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222359799" />
    <a title="Dija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2857113-dija"><img alt="Dija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360335537p2/2857113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222359799?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dija" href="/user/show/2857113-dija">Dija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525425915" href="/book/show/12842115-just-one-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=jan-2013">jan-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=wow">wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=authors-i-stalk">authors-i-stalk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=awww">awww</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=cotton-candy-fluff">cotton-candy-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222359799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5394746253756571337"><b>3.7/5 stars</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>Being a <i>huge</i> fan of Forman's, I was absolutely ecstatic when I heard she'd be writing another 2-book story centered around a couple and told from both their POVs. I'm happy (and more than a little relieved, considering my track record so far this year) to report that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842115.Just_One_Day__Just_One_Day___1_' title='Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Just One Day</a> lives up to the hype, and while I had a few minor problems with the story, I still ended up immensely enjoying it.<br/><br/>I wasn't too impressed with Allyson at the beginning, and with "Lulu" even less. </span>
  <span id="freeText5394746253756571337" style="display:none"><b>3.7/5 stars</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Being a <i>huge</i> fan of Forman's, I was absolutely ecstatic when I heard she'd be writing another 2-book story centered around a couple and told from both their POVs. I'm happy (and more than a little relieved, considering my track record so far this year) to report that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842115.Just_One_Day__Just_One_Day___1_" title="Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Day</a> lives up to the hype, and while I had a few minor problems with the story, I still ended up immensely enjoying it.<br><br>I wasn't too impressed with Allyson at the beginning, and with "Lulu" even less. That didn't deter me from the book at all, however, because if there was one thing I was sure about getting into this, it was how Forman has a knack for making her readers become subtly yet intricately captivated by her characters and their lives. That certainly held true for Willem and Allyson, and despite those aforementioned issues I had, I'm looking forward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842134.Just_One_Year__Just_One_Day___2_" title="Just One Year (Just One Day, #2) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Year</a> with even more fervor than I did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842115.Just_One_Day__Just_One_Day___1_" title="Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Day</a>. <br><br>There are too many unknowns about Willem for me to be 100% sure I love him, but I will say this: I am absolutely and completely in love with the Willem Lulu met and fell for. As for the rest, I'll reserve judgment until I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842134.Just_One_Year__Just_One_Day___2_" title="Just One Year (Just One Day, #2) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Year</a> and heard his side of things.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Who takes care of you now?”<br>At first I’m not sure I said it aloud and, if I did, that he heard me, because he doesn’t answer for a long time. But then finally, he says, “I take care of me.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Willem and Allyson are simply beautiful together. The magnetic attraction between them is apparent from their first meeting and it only gets more intense as they get to know each other properly. I loved reading their dialogue and witnessing them slowly fall in love. Even knowing they'd separate after just one day, I couldn't prevent myself from becoming invested in their romance. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>And that's when I understand that I have been stained. Whether I'm still in love with him, whether he was ever in love with me, and no matter who he's in love with now, Willem changed my life. He showed me how to get lost, and then I showed myself how to get found.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>The writing is dazzling with its depiction of life in Paris and the historical sites there and in neighboring countries. The setting shifts from London to Paris to America to all over Europe once again and the writing adds an almost mystical atmosphere to these well-known places. For me, this book had the feel of a revered black&amp;white movie, despite how vibrant and colorful the story is. <br><br>Overall, this was not as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay__If_I_Stay___1_" title="If I Stay (If I Stay, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a>, nor was I expecting it to be because epic stories like <i>that</i> only come around once in a while. Nonetheless, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842115.Just_One_Day__Just_One_Day___1_" title="Just One Day (Just One Day, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Day</a> is an exquisite depiction of first love and the uncertainties, risks, and hopes that come with it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842134.Just_One_Year__Just_One_Day___2_" title="Just One Year (Just One Day, #2) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Just One Year</a> can't get here fast enough!<br><br><b>For more reviews, visit my blog:<br> <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340428i/696822.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5394746253756571337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9uxPSpMiwfbEM+KNiToiKPkHTo9wDz2HmFS7KOxfggzMyiaYKHwInmMYVux+zyj3L1ipR76Cs+DDKv2ZIRxwlg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZfH+onXnd89M7vm532UDx12ieR6Km4ucoGWU/5vxzEtf15dwzrm+p+vFTdgokAkYi/2e1kQWBfv7G9JOVrI+0Q==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer2441774280785954267">Award-winning author and journalist Gayle Forman has written several bestselling novels for young adults, including the Just One Series, I Was Here, Where She Went and the #1 New York Times bestseller If I Stay, which has been translated into more than 40 languages and in 2014 was adapted into a major motion picture. <br/><br/>Gayle published Leave Me, her first novel starring adults in 2016 and her latest </span>
  <span id="freeText2441774280785954267" style="display:none">Award-winning author and journalist Gayle Forman has written several bestselling novels for young adults, including the Just One Series, I Was Here, Where She Went and the #1 New York Times bestseller If I Stay, which has been translated into more than 40 languages and in 2014 was adapted into a major motion picture. <br /><br />Gayle published Leave Me, her first novel starring adults in 2016 and her latest novel, I Have Lost My Way, comes out in March of 2018. <br /><br /><br />Gayle lives with her husband and daughters in Brooklyn.</span>
